Selling Before Measuring: The Hanafi Ruling of Fasid
Ruling on selling a purchased item before it is measured, with proof and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that selling a measured item before remeasuring renders the sale fasid, and distinguish between sales by measurement and by estimation.

Core Idea
Selling a purchased item before measuring it is fasid because of gharar — unless sold by estimation.

This passage addresses a common scenario in trade: a buyer purchases an item sold by measurement (e.g., wheat by volume) but then sells it before measuring it himself. The Hanafi school holds that such a sale is defective (fasid) even after possession, due to the potential gharar (uncertainty) in the exact quantity. The text also discusses exceptions for real estate and estimation-based sales, along with an intra-Hanafi disagreement on counted items. Understanding this rule helps avoid invalid contracts in everyday transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Start by recognising what the passage is about: a person buys something measured (kayliyan kaylan). What is the ruling on selling or consuming it before the buyer remeasures it? The matn states he should not sell or eat until he measures.
The act is selling before own measurement, not before taking possession.
2
Locate the dalil and its 'illa
The commentary cites the hadith 'Do not sell anything until you take possession.' This hadith is explained (mu'allal) by the presence of gharar from possible contract dissolution due to destruction. Understand that the 'illa is the risk of destruction for movables.
The gharar here is not about quantity but about the possibility that the sold item might be destroyed before the buyer takes possession, thus voiding the contract.
3
Analyse the exception for real estate
The text contrasts movables (frequent destruction) with real estate (rare destruction). This leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad applies the hadith literally, disallowing sale before possession even for real estate. The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) allow it due to rarity of gharar.
This is a key thamarah al-khilaf: real estate can be sold before possession according to the majority.
4
Distinguish between sale by measurement and sale by estimation
The phrase 'by measurement' (kaylan) excludes mujazafah (sale by estimation). In a mujazafah sale, the buyer does not know the exact quantity; the excess over his assumption is not his. Therefore, once he takes possession, he can dispose of it without measuring. No gharar arises because the uncertainty was already present.
The ruling for mujazafah is valid without remeasurement.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on counted items
The text ends by citing Al-Jami' al-Saghir and Al-Mujtaba. All agree that selling a measured or weighed item before measurement renders the sale fasid. For counted items, Abu Hanifa treats them like weighed (fasid), while Sahibayn treat them like textiles (non-ribawi) but still the sale is fasid. The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa.
The disagreement is about the basis (ribawi vs non-ribawi), not the outcome (fasid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شرى كيلياً كيلاً لم يبعه ولم يأكله حتى يكيله
والهلاك فيما ينقلُ ويحول كثير، وفي العقار نادر فلهذا جاز البيع قبل قبض المبيع في المنقولات لا في العقار.
[1] قوله : نهى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن بيع ما لم يقبض معلل بأن فيه غرر انفساخ العقد تقدير الهلاك، والهلاك في العقار نادر، وعند محمد لا يجوز في العقار أيضاً عملاً بإطلاق النهي.
[2] والجواب عن الشيخين أن ركن البيع صدر من أهله في محله، ولا غرر فيه؛ لأن الهلاك في العقار نادر، بخلاف المنقول، والغرر المنهي عنه غرر انفساخ العقد، والحديث معلول به عملاً بدلائل الجواز.
[3] قوله : كيلاً؛ بخلاف ما إذا باعه مجازفةً، فإن الزائد على ما كان في ذهنه له فإذا قبضه جاز التصرف فيه، ولا حاجة إلى الكيل.
[4] قوله : لم يبعه، ولم يذكر المصنف حكم هذا البيع، وقد صرحوا بفساده في «الجامع الصغير»: محمد عن يعقوب عن أبي حنيفة قال: إذا اشتريت شيئاً مما يكال أو يوزن أو يعد فاشتريت ما يكال كيلاً، أو ما يوزن وزناً، وما يعد عداً، فلا تبعه حتى تكيله وتزنه وتعد، فإن بعته قبل أن تفعل، وقد قبضته فالبيع فاسد في الكيل والوزن. انتهى. وفي «المجتبى»: لو اشترى المعدود عداً، فكالموزون الحرمة الزيادة عليه، وعندهما كالذروع؛ لأنه ليس من الربويات ثمّ إن باعه فيما لم يخير بيعه كان فاسداً. انتهى.
And whoever buys something measurable by measurement, he should not sell it nor eat it until he measures it. And destruction in movable goods is frequent, and in real estate rare, so for this reason, sale before possession of the sold item is permissible in movables but not in real estate. [1] His saying: The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade selling what is not taken possession, it is explained that it contains gharar of dissolution of the contract due to estimated destruction, and destruction in real estate is rare, and according to Muhammad, it is not permissible even in real estate, acting on the general application of the prohibition. [2] The answer from the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the pillar of sale came from its people in its place, and there is no gharar in it because destruction in real estate is rare, unlike movable property, and the prohibited gharar is the gharar of dissolution of the contract, and the hadith is explained by this, acting on the proofs of permissibility. [3] His saying: 'by measurement' – unlike if he sells it by estimation, for then the excess over what he had in mind is not his, so when he takes possession, it becomes permissible to dispose of it, and there is no need for measurement. [4] His saying: 'he should not sell it', and the author did not mention the ruling of this sale; but they explicitly stated its corruption in 'Al-Jami' al-Saghir': Muhammad from Ya'qub from Abu Hanifa said: If you buy something that is measured or weighed or counted, and you buy it by measurement, weighing, or counting, do not sell it until you measure it, weigh it, or count it. If you sell it before doing that, even if you have taken possession, the sale is corrupt (fasid) in measurement and weight. End quote. And in 'Al-Mujtaba': If one buys counted items by count, it is like weighed items in the prohibition of increase, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is like textiles because it is not among ribawi items; then if he sells it without having the choice to sell, it is corrupt. End quote.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states: If someone buys an item that is sold by measurement (kaylīyan kaylan), he must not sell or consume it until he measures it. The commentary first connects this to the earlier discussion: destruction is frequent in movables and rare in real estate, which is why sale before possession is allowed for real estate but not movables. Then, the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ is cited: 'Do not sell anything until you take possession of it.' This hadith is explained by the gharar of contract dissolution on estimation of destruction. Imam Muhammad takes the general application of the hadith and holds that even real estate cannot be sold before possession. The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) respond: The pillar of the sale (the contract) is from its rightful parties and at its proper place, and there is no gharar here because destruction of real estate is rare. Thus the hadith is interpreted in light of the evidence for permissibility. The text then clarifies that 'by measurement' excludes selling by estimation (mujāzafah), where the exact quantity is unknown; there, the excess beyond what the buyer assumed in his mind is not his, so once he takes possession, he may dispose of it without needing to measure. Finally, the ruling on selling before measuring is given: Abu Hanifa says in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: If you buy something measured, weighed, or counted, do not sell it until you perform the respective measurement. If you sell before that, even if you have taken possession, the sale is fasid (corrupt) in measurement and weight. In Al-Mujtaba, it is added that for counted items, it is like weighed items regarding the prohibition of increase, and according to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), counted items are like textiles (non-ribawi), so the sale is fasid. This intra-Hanafi difference highlights that the needed measurement is a condition for validity. The overall ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah is that the sale is fasid, and the mufta bihi position is the general prohibition with the exception for real estate according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
كيلياً (kayliyan): An item that is sold by measurement (volume or weight) as per the contract.
مجازفة (mujāzafah): Selling without exact measurement, by estimation or guesswork.
ربويات (ribawiyyāt): Items subject to riba rules (e.g., gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) where increase is prohibited in hand-to-hand exchanges.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if someone buys a measured item (e.g., wheat by volume) and sells it before measuring it himself, even though he has taken possession?
A) The sale is valid because possession transfers ownership.
B) The sale is fasid (corrupt) and must be repeated with proper measurement.
C) The sale is batil (void) and has no effect.
D) The sale is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
Selling a purchased item before remeasuring it is a fasid sale; the only exceptions are real estate (per Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and mujazafah sales.

Selling Measured Goods Before Measuring: Prohibition, Conditions, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on the rule and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on selling kili goods before measuring and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding real estate.

Core Idea
A sale of kili goods before measuring is fasid; but real estate before possession is allowed by the two shaykhs due to rarity of destruction.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the Hanafi position on when measurement is required before selling goods. It establishes the default rule that measured goods must be measured before sale, but it also reveals an important intra-madhhab dispute about whether real estate is exempt from this requirement. Understanding this distinction is crucial for ensuring valid transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its basis
Find the explicit rule: 'Whoever buys something measured, he should not sell it until he measures it.' Note the reasoning: the Prophet prohibited selling before possession due to gharar (risk of rescission).
The hadith of Hakim ibn Hizam is cited.
2
Understand the exception for real estate
The text states that destruction is rare in real estate, so the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) allow selling real estate before possession. Imam Muhammad disagrees.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the opposing arguments
The two shaykhs argue the 'illa of gharar is absent in real estate. Muhammad argues the general prohibition applies without restriction.
The hadith is 'Do not sell anything until you take possession.'
4
Apply the condition of measurement
The condition that the seller measures after the sale in the presence of the buyer is explained: if measured before the sale, it is not considered.
This ensures both parties know the exact quantity.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the two shaykhs, permitting real estate sale before possession, as per al-Hidayah.
Authority weight: zahir riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع / باب الإقالة والمرابحة والتولية
ومَن شَرَى كيلياً كيلاً لم يبعه ولم يأكله حتى يكيله
على أن نَهْي النَّبيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم عن بيع ما لم يُقْبَضُ مُعلَّل بأنَّ فِيهِ غَرَرَ انفساخ العقد تقدير الهلاك، والهلاك في العقار نادر، وعند محمد لا يجوز في العقار أيضاً عملاً بإطلاق النَّهْي. ومَن شَرَى كيلياً كيلاً: أي بشرط الكيل، لم يبعه ولم يأكله حتى يكيله) والهلاك فيما ينقلُ ويحول كثير، وفي العقار نادر فلهذا جاز البيع قبل قبض المبيع في المنقولات لا في العقار. قوله: نهى النبي أخرج النسائي في سننه الكبرى عن حكيم بن حزام قال: «قلت: يا رسول الله؛ إنّي رجل ابتاع هذه البيوع وأبيعها، فما يحل لي هاهنا، وما يحرم؟ قال: لا تبيعنَّ شيئاً حتى تقبضه» (١)، كذا في نصب الراية (٢). قوله: عند محمد والجواب عن الشيخين أنَّ ركن البيع صدرَ من أهلِهِ في محله، ولا غرر فيه؛ لأنَّ الهلاك في العقار نادر، بخلاف المنقول، والغرر المنهي عنه غررُ انفساخ العقد، والحديث معلول به عملاً بدلائل الجواز، كذا في «الهداية»(۳). قوله: كيلاً؛ بخلاف ما إذا باعه مجازفةً، فإنَّ الزائد على ما كان في ذهنه له فإذا قبضه جاز التصرُّف فيه، ولا حاجة إلى الكيل. قوله: لم يبعه، ولم يذكر المصنف حكم هذا البيع، وقد صرحوا بفساده في «الجامع الصغير»: محمد عن يعقوب عن أبي حنيفة قال: إذا اشتريت شيئاً مما يكال أو يوزن أو يعد فاشتريت ما يكال كيلاً، أو ما يوزن وزناً، وما يعد عداً، فلا تبعه حتى تكيله وتزنه وتعد، فإن بعته قبل أن تفعل، وقد قبضته فالبيع فاسد في الكيل والوزن. انتهى. وفي «المجتبى»: لو اشترى المعدود عداً، فكالموزون الحرمة الزيادة عليه، وعندهما كالذروع؛ لأنه ليس من الربويات ثمّ إن باعه فيما لم يخير بيعه كان فاسداً. انتهى. (۱) في «سنن النسائي الكبرى» (٤): (٣۷)، و«صحيح ابن حبان» (۱۱): ٣٥٨)، و«المجتبى»(۷: ٢٨٦)، وغيرها. (۲) «نصب الراية» (٤: ٣٢). (۳) «الهداية»(۳: ٥٩).
وشرط كيلُ البائع بعد بيعه بحضرة المشتري
زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية
فإنَّه «نهى عن بيع الطعام حتى يجري فيه صاعان صاعُ البائع، وصاع المشتري».
(وشرط كيلُ البائع بعد بيعه بحضرة المشتري) حتى إن كاله البائع قبل البيع فلا اعتبار له وإن كال البائع بحضرة المشتري: وعندهما كالذروع؛ لأنه ليس من الربويات ثمّ إن باعه فيما لم يخير بيعه كان فاسداً. انتهى. قوله: فإنه ... الخ أخرجه ابن ماجة في «سننه» عن جابر مرفوعاً إلى النبي، والدليل العقلي على عدم جوازه بدون الكيل أنَّ المكيل يحتمل الزيادة على المشروط، وهو للبائع لا يجوز التصرُّفُ في مال الغير، فيجب التحرُّزُ عنه بترك التصرُّف. قوله: صاعُ البائع ... الخ؛ أراد بصاع البائع صاعه لنفسه حين يشتريه، وبصاع المشتري صاعه لنفسه حين يبيعه؛ لإجماعهم على أنَّ البيع الواحد لا يحتاج إلى الكيل مرتين، كذا في «البناية» (٢). قوله: لا اعتبار له، ولو كان بحضرة المشتري؛ لأنه ليس صاعُ البائع ولا المشتري، والشرط أن يوجد الصاعان منهما بالحديث ذكره شيخنا العلامة الطحطاوي في «حاشية الدر المختار» (۳). وإنما شرط ذلك؛ لأنَّ البيع يتناولُ ما يجوز الكيل أو الوزن، وهو مجهول، فربّما يزيد وينقص، فما لم يكل لنفسه أو لم يزن لا يمتاز المبيع عن غيره، فكان البيع مجهولاً. (1) من حديث جابر وأبي هريرة وأنس وابن عباس في سنن ابن ماجه (۲): ٧٥٠)، و«سنن البيهقي الكبير»(٥: ۳۱۵)، قال البيهقي: روي موصولاً من أوجه إذا ضم بعضها إلى بعض قوي مع ما ثبت عن ابن عمر وابن عباس، وينظر: «المصباح» (۳): (٢٤)، و«التلخيص»(۳: ۲۷)، و«نصب الراية» (٤: ٣٤)، وغيرها. (۲) «البناية» (٦: ٥١١). (۳) «حاشية الطحطاوي» (۳: ۱۰۱).
Book of Sales / Chapter of Iqalah and Murabahah and Tawliyah. And whoever buys something measured by measurement, he should not sell it nor eat it until he measures it. [Commentary: The Prophet's prohibition of selling what has not been taken possession is reasoned by the fact that it contains the gharar of the contract being rescinded due to estimated destruction. Destruction in real estate is rare, and according to Muhammad, it is not permissible in real estate either, acting on the general application of the prohibition. And whoever buys something measured by measurement: i.e., conditioned upon measurement, he should not sell it nor eat it until he measures it. Destruction in movable property is frequent, and in real estate it is rare, so selling before taking possession is permitted in movables, not in real estate. He says: The Prophet's prohibition – Al-Nasa'i recorded in his Sunan al-Kubra from Hakim ibn Hizam who said: I said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I am a man who trades in these transactions and sells them. So what is lawful for me here and what is unlawful?' He said: 'Do not sell anything until you take possession of it,' recorded in Nasb al-Rayah. He says: Regarding Muhammad and the answer to the two shaykhs: The pillar of the sale issued from its people in its place, and there is no gharar in it because destruction in real estate is rare, unlike movable property, and the prohibited gharar is the gharar of the contract being rescinded, and the hadith is reasoned with this acting on the proofs of permissibility, as in al-Hidayah. He says: 'by measurement'; as opposed to if he sells it estimated, then the excess over what was in his mind belongs to him, so when he takes possession, disposal in it is permitted, and there is no need for measurement. He says: 'he should not sell it,' and the author did not mention the ruling of this sale, and they declared it void in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Muhammad from Ya'qub from Abu Hanifa said: If you buy something that is measured or weighed or counted, and you buy what is measured by measurement, or what is weighed by weight, and what is counted by count, do not sell it until you measure it, weigh it, and count it. If you sell it before doing that, and you have taken possession, then the sale is void in measurement and weight. End. And in al-Mujtaba: If one buys something counted by count, then it is like what is weighed regarding the prohibition of excess, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is like lengths of cloth because it is not from ribawi items. Then if he sells it without option, the sale is void. End. (1) In Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra (4): 37, and Sahih Ibn Hibban (11): 358, and al-Mujtaba (7): 286, and others. (2) Nasb al-Rayah (4:32). (3) al-Hidayah (3:59). And the condition that the seller measures after his sale in the presence of the buyer. Zubdat al-Nihayah li 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. He said: 'He forbade selling food until two measures pass: the seller's measure and the buyer's measure.' (And the condition that the seller measures after his sale in the presence of the buyer) so that if the seller measured it before the sale, it is not considered, even if the seller measured it in the presence of the buyer: and according to the two it is like lengths of cloth because it is not from ribawi items. Then if he sells it without option, the sale is void. End. He says: 'He said... etc.' Ibn Majah recorded in his Sunan from Jabir raised to the Prophet, and the rational proof for its impermissibility without measurement is that measured items may exceed the stipulated amount, and it belongs to the seller, so disposal of another's property is not permitted, so precaution is necessary by refraining from disposal. He says: 'the seller's measure... etc.'; he intended by 'the seller's measure' his measure for himself when he buys, and by 'the buyer's measure' his measure for himself when he sells; because of their consensus that a single sale does not require measurement twice, as in al-Binayah (2). He says: 'it is not considered, even if it was in the presence of the buyer'; because it is neither the seller's measure nor the buyer's measure, and the condition is that the two measures come from them according to the hadith, mentioned by our teacher al-Tahtawi in Hashiyat al-Durr al-Mukhtar (3). And this condition is stipulated because the sale involves what is subject to measurement or weight, and it is unknown, so it may increase or decrease. As long as he has not measured for himself or weighed, the sold item is not distinguished from others, so the sale would be unknown. (1) From the hadith of Jabir, Abu Huraira, Anas, and Ibn Abbas in Sunan Ibn Majah (2): 750, and Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir (5): 315; al-Bayhaqi said: It is narrated as connected from several paths, and when combined they strengthen it along with what is confirmed from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas. And refer to al-Misbah (3): 24, and al-Talkhis (3): 27, and Nasb al-Rayah (4): 34, and others. (2) al-Binayah (6:511). (3) Hashiyat al-Tahtawi (3:101).
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is an expansion commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on the ruling of selling measured (kili) goods before actually measuring them. The author begins by stating the rule: whoever buys something that is habitually measured (like grains) must not sell it or consume it until he measures it. The reason is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited selling what one has not taken possession of, and this prohibition is reasoned by the gharar (risk) that the contract might be rescinded due to destruction of the item before delivery. In movable goods, destruction is frequent, so the gharar is significant; in real estate, destruction is rare, so the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) allowed selling real estate before possession. However, Imam Muhammad held that the general prohibition applies even to real estate. The text then cites the hadith of Hakim ibn Hizam as evidence for the prohibition. The commentary explains that the two shaykhs answer Muhammad by arguing that the sale is sound because the pillar of the contract was complete, and there is no gharar in real estate due to rarity of destruction. The gharar prohibited is specifically the gharar of rescission, which is absent here. Next, the text discusses that the condition of measuring applies only when the item was purchased with the condition of measurement; if purchased estimated (mujazafah), measurement is not required. The author then notes that the matn did not state the ruling if one sells before measuring, but the earlier Hanafi authorities like al-Jami' al-Saghir explicitly say such a sale is fasid (void). In al-Mujtaba, a similar ruling is given for counted items. The second part of the passage addresses the condition that the seller must measure the item after the sale in the presence of the buyer. The hadith of Jabir mentions two measures: the seller's measure when he bought it and the buyer's measure when he sells it. If the seller measured before the sale, that measurement is not considered because it is not the measure of the seller (for his own purchase) or the buyer (for his own sale). The rational basis is that a kili item may exceed the stipulated amount, giving the seller an unfair advantage; measuring ensures the item is known and the transaction is free from gharar. Overall, the passage clarifies the nuanced Hanafi position on when measurement is required and the intra-madhhab difference regarding real estate.

Key Terms
كيلياً (kiliyyan): Something sold by measurement of volume (e.g., grains). It is contrasted with 'adadiyyan (by count) and wazniyyan (by weight).
قبض (qabd): Physical taking of possession; the buyer's control over the item.
غرر (gharar): Risk or uncertainty that may lead to dispute; in this context, the risk that the contract would be rescinded due to destruction before delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad (within the Hanafi school), is it permissible to sell a house before taking physical possession of it?
A) Yes, it is permissible because the prohibition is only for movable goods.
B) No, it is not permissible because the general hadith prohibits selling anything before possession.
C) Yes, it is permissible because real estate is not subject to gharar.
D) No, it is not permissible only if the house is measured by volume.

Key Takeaway
The sale of kili goods before measuring is fasid, but real estate before possession is allowed by the majority of the Hanafi school due to the absence of gharar.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
15 min
Condition of Seller's Measurement After Sale
Ruling with proof: condition of measurement after sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of measurement after a sale, apply it to foodstuff, and distinguish items that require double measurement from those that do not.

Core Idea
A sale of foodstuff is invalid unless the seller measures after the contract in the buyer's presence.

This passage addresses a crucial condition for the validity of sales of measured goods: the seller must re-measure the item after concluding the sale, and in the presence of the buyer. This requirement, based on a hadith and rational reasoning, aims to eliminate uncertainty about the exact quantity delivered. The text also discusses exceptions for items sold by length and the special case of salam transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Read the opening statement: 'The condition is the seller's measurement after his sale in the presence of the buyer.' Determine what the condition is and what happens if it is not fulfilled (the sale is fasid).
The condition is a shart for validity, not a rukn.
2
Examine the hadith proof
Look at the hadith cited: 'The Prophet forbade the sale of food until two measures pass: the seller's and the buyer's.' Identify the legal implication (wahj al-dalalah): the prohibition indicates the sale is invalid without two measures.
The hadith is from Sunan Ibn Majah and is zanni al-thubut but qati' al-dalalah in this context.
3
Analyze the rational proof
The text provides a rational argument: a measured item may contain more than what was stipulated, and that excess belongs to the seller; thus, without measurement, the transaction involves uncertainty (jahalah) and potential consumption of another's property without consent.
This is a 'illa (effective cause) for the condition.
4
Distinguish items that require double measurement
Identify which goods require the seller's measurement after sale: items sold by volume (kayl), weight (wazn), or count (add). Note that items sold by length (dhi'ra') are exempt because any increase or decrease is for the buyer's account.
This distinction is based on the Sahibayn's view; Abu Hanifa may have held differently but the relied-upon position is the exemption.
5
Understand the exception in salam
The passage mentions a special case in salam transactions where two sales combine, requiring two separate measurements. This is an exception to the general rule that a single sale needs only one measurement (by the seller after the contract).
This exception is explained in the chapter of Salam and is not part of the general rule.

وشرط كيلُ البائع بعد بيعه بحضرة المشتري
فإنَّه «نهى عن بيع الطعام حتى يجري فيه صاعان صاعُ البائع"، وصاع المشتري».
(وشرط كيلُ البائع بعد بيعه بحضرة المشتري) حتى إن كاله البائع قبل البيع فلا اعتبار له وإن كال البائع بحضرة المشتري : وعندهما كالذروع ؛ لأنه ليس من الربويات ثمّ إن باعه فيما لم يخير بيعه كان فاسداً. انتهى.
قوله : فإنه ... الخ أخرجه ابن ماجة في «سننه»: عن جابر مرفوعاً إلى النبي ، والدليل العقلي على عدم جوازه بدون الكيل أنَّ المكيل يحتمل الزيادة على المشروط، وهو للبائع لا يجوز التصرُّفُ في مال الغير، فيجب التحرُّزُ عنه بترك التصرُّف.
قوله : صاعُ البائع ... الخ ؛ أراد بصاع البائع صاعه لنفسه حين يشتريه، وبصاع المشتري صاعه لنفسه حين يبيعه ؛ لإجماعهم على أنَّ البيع الواحد لا يحتاج إلى الكيل مرتين، كذا في «البناية».
قوله : لا اعتبار له، ولو كان بحضرة المشتري ؛ لأنه ليس صاعُ البائع ولا المشتري ، والشرط أن يوجد الصاعان منهما بالحديث ذكره شيخنا العلامة الطحطاوي في «حاشية الدر المختار».
وإنما شرط ذلك ؛ لأنَّ البيع يتناولُ ما يجوز الكيل أو الوزن، وهو مجهول، فربّما يزيد وينقص، فما لم يكل لنفسه أو لم يزن لا يمتاز المبيع عن غيره، فكان البيع مجهولاً، كذا ما يُوزَنُ وما يعد، لا ما يذرعُ
وكذا إن كاله بعد البيع بغيبة المشتري ، كفى به في الصحيح ) : أي إن كال البائع بعد البيع بحضرة المشتري فهذا كاف ، ولا يشترط أن يكيل المشتري بعد ذلك، ومحمل الحديث المذكورِ ما إذا اجتمع الصفقتان بشرط الكيل على ما سيأتي في «باب السلم»، وهو ما إذا أسلم في كرِّبُر فلما حلَّ الأجل اشترى المسلم إليه من رجلٍ كُرّاً، أو أَمَرَ ربَّ السَّلم أن يقبضَهُ له ، ثم يقبضُهُ لنفسه، فاكتالَهُ له ، ثُمَّ اكتالَهُ لنفسه جاز"۔
(وكذا ما يُوزَنُ وما يعد ) : أي لا يبيعُهُ ولا يأكلُهُ حتى يزنَهُ أو يعدَّهُ ثانياً ، ويكفي وزنُهُ إن وزنَهُ ، أو عده بعد البيع بحضرة المشتري. (لا ما يذرعُ) : أي لا يشترط ما ذُكِرَ في المذروعاتِ ثانياً. فيفسد البيع، كذا في «الكفاية». قوله : وكذا ...الخ ؛ أي وكذا لا اعتبار له إن كان بعد البيع بغيبة المشتري ؛ لأنَّ الكيل من تمام التسليم، ولا تسليم مع الغيبة. قوله : في الصحيح؛ رد لما قيل : شرط كيلان، كيلُ البائع بعد العقد بحضرة المشتري، وكيل المشتري قبل التصرُّف فيه، ولا يكتفى بكيل البائع فقط ؛ لظاهر الحديث، فإنّه اعتبر صاعين. قوله : كاف ؛ لأنَّ المبيع صار معلوماً بمكيل واحد، وتحقق معنى التسليم، كذا في «البحر». قوله : جاز ؛ أي لا يصح إلا بصاعين ؛ لاجتماع الصفقتين بشرط الكيل : أحدهما : شراء المسلم إليه. وثانيهما: قبض ربِّ المُسَلَّم لنفسه، وهو كالبيع الجديد، فتجتمع صفتان. قوله : وما يعد ؛ غيرُ الدَّراهم والدنانير ؛ لأنه يجوز التصرُّف فيهما بعد القبض قبل العد كما صرحوا به. قوله : لا يشترط ... الخ ؛ لأنَّ الزيادة للمشتري، فإنّ الذرع وصف في الثوب،
And the condition is the seller's measurement after his sale in the presence of the buyer. Verily, he (the Prophet) forbade the sale of food until two measures pass in it: the seller's measure and the buyer's measure. (And the condition is the seller's measurement after his sale in the presence of the buyer) such that if the seller measured before the sale, it is not considered, and if the seller measured in the presence of the buyer: and according to the two companions, it is like the dhi'ra' items; because it is not from ribawi items. Then if he sold it without giving him an option, the sale is void. End. His statement: Verily... etc. was reported by Ibn Majah in his Sunan from Jabir raised to the Prophet, and the rational evidence for its non-permissibility without measurement is that a measured item may exceed what is stipulated, and it belongs to the seller, so dealing with another's property is not permissible, thus one must guard against it by refraining from dealing. His statement: The seller's measure... etc.; he meant by the seller's measure his measure for himself when he buys it, and by the buyer's measure his measure for himself when he sells it; due to their consensus that a single sale does not need two measurements, as in al-Binaya. His statement: It is not considered, even if in the presence of the buyer; because it is neither the seller's measure nor the buyer's, and the condition is that the two measures exist from them according to the hadith, mentioned by our teacher al-Tahtawi in Hashiyat al-Durr al-Mukhtar. And why this condition? Because the sale includes what is permissible to measure or weigh, and it is unknown, so it may increase or decrease, so as long as he does not measure for himself or weigh, the sold item is not distinguished from others, so the sale is unknown. Similarly for what is weighed and counted, not for what is measured by length. (And similarly if he measured after the sale in the absence of the buyer, it suffices according to the sound view): i.e., if the seller measured after the sale in the presence of the buyer, it is sufficient, and the buyer does not need to measure thereafter. And the interpretation of the aforementioned hadith is when two transactions come together with the condition of measurement, as will come in the chapter of Salam, which is when one pays salam in a kur of burr, then when the term comes, the muslam ilayh buys a kur from a man, or commands the owner of the salam to take possession for him, then takes possession for himself, so he measures it for him, then measures it for himself, it is permissible. (And similarly what is weighed and counted): i.e., he does not sell it nor consume it until he weighs it or counts it a second time, and his weighing suffices if he weighs it, or his counting after the sale in the presence of the buyer. (Not what is measured by length): i.e., what was mentioned for measured-by-length items a second time is not required. So the sale is void. As in al-Kifaya. His statement: And similarly... etc.; i.e., similarly it is not considered if it was after the sale in the absence of the buyer; because measurement is part of complete delivery, and there is no delivery with absence. His statement: according to the sound view; a refutation of what was said: two measurements are required, the seller's measurement after the contract in the presence of the buyer, and the buyer's measurement before disposal of it, and the seller's measurement alone is not sufficient; due to the apparent meaning of the hadith, for it considered two measures. His statement: sufficient; because the sold item became known by one measurement, and the meaning of delivery is realized, as in al-Bahr. His statement: permissible; i.e., it is not valid except with two measures; because two transactions come together with the condition of measurement: one is the purchase of the muslam ilayh, and the second is the taking possession of the owner of the salam for himself, and it is like a new sale, so two qualities come together. His statement: and what is counted; other than dirhams and dinars; because disposal of them after possession before counting is permissible as they have stated. His statement: not required... etc.; because the increase is for the buyer, for the length is a description in the cloth.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on the necessity of double measurement in the sale of foodstuff and similar items. It first states the condition: the seller must measure the item after concluding the sale and in the presence of the buyer. The hadith proof is the Prophet's prohibition of selling food until two measures pass: the seller's and the buyer's. The rational proof is that a measured item may contain more than stipulated, and since the seller cannot dispose of another's property, this risk must be avoided by proper measurement. The commentary clarifies that if the seller measured before the sale, it is invalid, because it is neither the seller's measure (for himself when buying) nor the buyer's measure (for himself when selling). The sound view is that if the seller measures after the sale even in the buyer's absence, it suffices, because measurement is part of delivery, and delivery can occur in absence. For weighed and counted items, the same rule applies: a second weighing or counting after the sale is required if done in the buyer's presence. However, items sold by length (like cloth) do not require this double measurement, because a decrease or increase in length is for the buyer's account (the seller takes the risk of loss). The passage also discusses a special case in salam: when the muslam ilayh buys a kur and then the buyer takes possession for himself, two measurements are needed because two transactions combine.

Key Terms
الكيل (al-kayl): The act of measuring volume, specifically for grain-like foodstuffs.
صاع (sa'): A unit of measure for dry goods; here it refers to the seller's measure and the buyer's measure.
الذرع (al-dhi'ra'): Measurement by length (e.g., cloth). The condition of double measurement does not apply to such items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following items does NOT require the seller to measure after the sale?
A) A sack of rice sold by weight
B) A piece of cloth sold by length
C) A bushel of apples sold by count
D) A barrel of olive oil sold by volume

Key Takeaway
The seller must measure after the contract in the buyer's presence for kayl, wazn, and add items; length items are exempt.
